# Antigravity + Gemini CLI OAuth Plugin for Opencode

[](#antigravity--gemini-cli-oauth-plugin-for-opencode)

[![npm version](https://camo.githubusercontent.com/02bbc80b2f1f0d4eb639134c616929e2d15298107193832c59cf25512c4b63e6/68747470733a2f2f696d672e736869656c64732e696f2f6e706d2f762f6f70656e636f64652d616e7469677261766974792d617574682e737667)](https://www.npmjs.com/package/opencode-antigravity-auth) [![npm beta](https://camo.githubusercontent.com/8e8e573b1ab770d513e09bc67e906dabf454c453a6aaf64b78b44e1007b5b90d/68747470733a2f2f696d672e736869656c64732e696f2f6e706d2f762f6f70656e636f64652d616e7469677261766974792d617574682f626574612e7376673f6c6162656c3d62657461)](https://www.npmjs.com/package/opencode-antigravity-auth) [![npm downloads](https://camo.githubusercontent.com/d560625fcaa5cdef8df9dac667c11dbf33cd4ba31dd110233e0883590af4a1ea/68747470733a2f2f696d672e736869656c64732e696f2f6e706d2f64772f6f70656e636f64652d616e7469677261766974792d617574682e737667)](https://www.npmjs.com/package/opencode-antigravity-auth) [![License: MIT](https://camo.githubusercontent.com/fdf2982b9f5d7489dcf44570e714e3a15fce6253e0cc6b5aa61a075aac2ff71b/68747470733a2f2f696d672e736869656c64732e696f2f62616467652f4c6963656e73652d4d49542d79656c6c6f772e737667)](/NoeFabris/opencode-antigravity-auth/blob/main/LICENSE) [![X (Twitter)](https://camo.githubusercontent.com/debaa0f8ac0c20d22c8993c48698b3c460e9667a097c055a3872311840dd6ead/68747470733a2f2f696d672e736869656c64732e696f2f62616467652f582d40646f706573616c6d6f6e2d3030303030303f7374796c653d666c6174266c6f676f3d78)](https://x.com/dopesalmon)

Enable Opencode to authenticate against **Antigravity** (Google's IDE) via OAuth so you can use Antigravity rate limits and access models like `gemini-3.1-pro` and `claude-opus-4-6-thinking` with your Google credentials.

## What You Get

[](#what-you-get)

-   **Claude Opus 4.6, Sonnet 4.6** and **Gemini 3.1 Pro/Flash** via Google OAuth
-   **Multi-account support** — add multiple Google accounts, auto-rotates when rate-limited
-   **Dual quota system** — access both Antigravity and Gemini CLI quotas from one plugin
-   **Thinking models** — extended thinking for Claude and Gemini 3 with configurable budgets
-   **Google Search grounding** — enable web search for Gemini models (auto or always-on)
-   **Auto-recovery** — handles session errors and tool failures automatically
-   **Plugin compatible** — works alongside other OpenCode plugins (oh-my-opencode, dcp, etc.)

---

**⚠️ Terms of Service Warning — Read Before Installing**

> \[!CAUTION\] Using this plugin (and any proxy for antgravity) violate Google's Terms of Service. A number of users have reported their Google accounts being **banned** or **shadow-banned** (restricted access without explicit notification).
> 
> **By using this plugin, you acknowledge:**
> 
> -   This is an unofficial tool not endorsed by Google
> -   Your account may be suspended or permanently banned
> -   You assume all risks associated with using this plugin

---

## Installation

[](#installation)

**For Humans**

**Option A: Let an LLM do it**

Paste this into any LLM agent (Claude Code, OpenCode, Cursor, etc.):

```
Install the opencode-antigravity-auth plugin and add the Antigravity model definitions to ~/.config/opencode/opencode.json by following: https://raw.githubusercontent.com/NoeFabris/opencode-antigravity-auth/dev/README.md
```

**Option B: Manual setup**

1.  **Add the plugin** to `~/.config/opencode/opencode.json`:
    
    {
      "plugin": \["opencode-antigravity-auth@latest"\]
    }
    
    > Want bleeding-edge features? Use `opencode-antigravity-auth@beta` instead.
    
2.  **Login** with your Google account:
    
    opencode auth login
    
3.  **Add models** — choose one:
    
    -   Run `opencode auth login` → Google → OAuth with Google (Antigravity) → select **"Configure models in opencode.json"** (auto-configures all models)
    -   Or manually copy the [full configuration](#models) below
4.  **Use it:**
    
    opencode run "Hello" --model=google/antigravity-claude-opus-4-6-thinking --variant=max
    

**For LLM Agents**

### Step-by-Step Instructions

[](#step-by-step-instructions)

1.  Edit the OpenCode configuration file at `~/.config/opencode/opencode.json`
    
    > **Note**: This path works on all platforms. On Windows, `~` resolves to your user home directory (e.g., `C:\Users\YourName`).
    
2.  Add the plugin to the `plugin` array
    
3.  Add the model definitions from the [Full models configuration](#models) section
    
4.  Set `provider` to `"google"` and choose a model
    

### Verification

[](#verification)

opencode run "Hello" --model=google/antigravity-claude-opus-4-6-thinking --variant=max

---

## Models

[](#models)

### Model Reference

[](#model-reference)

**Antigravity quota** (default routing for Claude and Gemini):

Model

Variants

Notes

`antigravity-gemini-3-pro`

low, high

Gemini 3 Pro with thinking

`antigravity-gemini-3.1-pro`

low, high

Gemini 3.1 Pro with thinking (rollout-dependent)

`antigravity-gemini-3-flash`

minimal, low, medium, high

Gemini 3 Flash with thinking

`antigravity-claude-sonnet-4-6`

—

Claude Sonnet 4.6

`antigravity-claude-opus-4-6-thinking`

low, max

Claude Opus 4.6 with extended thinking

**Gemini CLI quota** (separate from Antigravity; used when `cli_first` is true or as fallback):

Model

Notes

`gemini-2.5-flash`

Gemini 2.5 Flash

`gemini-2.5-pro`

Gemini 2.5 Pro

`gemini-3-flash-preview`

Gemini 3 Flash (preview)

`gemini-3-pro-preview`

Gemini 3 Pro (preview)

`gemini-3.1-pro-preview`

Gemini 3.1 Pro (preview, rollout-dependent)

`gemini-3.1-pro-preview-customtools`

Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview Custom Tools (preview, rollout-dependent)

> **Routing Behavior:**
> 
> -   **Antigravity-first (default):** Gemini models use Antigravity quota across accounts.
> -   **CLI-first (`cli_first: true`):** Gemini models use Gemini CLI quota first.
> -   When a Gemini quota pool is exhausted, the plugin automatically falls back to the other pool.
> -   Claude and image models always use Antigravity. Model names are automatically transformed for the target API (e.g., `antigravity-gemini-3-flash` → `gemini-3-flash-preview` for CLI).

**Using variants:**

opencode run "Hello" --model=google/antigravity-claude-opus-4-6-thinking --variant=max

For details on variant configuration and thinking levels, see [docs/MODEL-VARIANTS.md](/NoeFabris/opencode-antigravity-auth/blob/main/docs/MODEL-VARIANTS.md).

**Full models configuration (copy-paste ready)**

Add this to your `~/.config/opencode/opencode.json`:

{
  "$schema": "https://opencode.ai/config.json",
  "plugin": \["opencode-antigravity-auth@latest"\],
  "provider": {
    "google": {
      "models": {
        "antigravity-gemini-3-pro": {
          "name": "Gemini 3 Pro (Antigravity)",
          "limit": { "context": 1048576, "output": 65535 },
          "modalities": { "input": \["text", "image", "pdf"\], "output": \["text"\] },
          "variants": {
            "low": { "thinkingLevel": "low" },
            "high": { "thinkingLevel": "high" }
          }
        },
        "antigravity-gemini-3.1-pro": {
          "name": "Gemini 3.1 Pro (Antigravity)",
          "limit": { "context": 1048576, "output": 65535 },
          "modalities": { "input": \["text", "image", "pdf"\], "output": \["text"\] },
          "variants": {
            "low": { "thinkingLevel": "low" },
            "high": { "thinkingLevel": "high" }
          }
        },
        "antigravity-gemini-3-flash": {
          "name": "Gemini 3 Flash (Antigravity)",
          "limit": { "context": 1048576, "output": 65536 },
          "modalities": { "input": \["text", "image", "pdf"\], "output": \["text"\] },
          "variants": {
            "minimal": { "thinkingLevel": "minimal" },
            "low": { "thinkingLevel": "low" },
            "medium": { "thinkingLevel": "medium" },
            "high": { "thinkingLevel": "high" }
          }
        },
        "antigravity-claude-sonnet-4-6": {
          "name": "Claude Sonnet 4.6 (Antigravity)",
          "limit": { "context": 200000, "output": 64000 },
          "modalities": { "input": \["text", "image", "pdf"\], "output": \["text"\] }
        },
        "antigravity-claude-opus-4-6-thinking": {
          "name": "Claude Opus 4.6 Thinking (Antigravity)",
          "limit": { "context": 200000, "output": 64000 },
          "modalities": { "input": \["text", "image", "pdf"\], "output": \["text"\] },
          "variants": {
            "low": { "thinkingConfig": { "thinkingBudget": 8192 } },
            "max": { "thinkingConfig": { "thinkingBudget": 32768 } }
          }
        },
        "gemini-2.5-flash": {
          "name": "Gemini 2.5 Flash (Gemini CLI)",
          "limit": { "context": 1048576, "output": 65536 },

        },
        "gemini-3.1-pro-preview": {
          "name": "Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview (Gemini CLI)",
          "limit": { "context": 1048576, "output": 65535 },
          "modalities": { "input": \["text", "image", "pdf"\], "output": \["text"\] }
        },
        "gemini-3.1-pro-preview-customtools": {
          "name": "Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview Custom Tools (Gemini CLI)",
          "limit": { "context": 1048576, "output": 65535 },
          "modalities": { "input": \["text", "image", "pdf"\], "output": \["text"\] }
        }
      }
    }
  }
}

> **Backward Compatibility:** Legacy model names with `antigravity-` prefix (e.g., `antigravity-gemini-3-flash`) still work. The plugin automatically handles model name transformation for both Antigravity and Gemini CLI APIs.

---

## Multi-Account Setup

[](#multi-account-setup)

Add multiple Google accounts for higher combined quotas. The plugin automatically rotates between accounts when one is rate-limited.

opencode auth login  # Run again to add more accounts

**Account management options (via `opencode auth login`):**

-   **Configure models** — Auto-configure all plugin models in opencode.json
-   **Check quotas** — View remaining API quota for each account
-   **Manage accounts** — Enable/disable specific accounts for rotation

For details on load balancing, dual quota pools, and account storage, see [docs/MULTI-ACCOUNT.md](/NoeFabris/opencode-antigravity-auth/blob/main/docs/MULTI-ACCOUNT.md).

---

## Troubleshoot

[](#troubleshoot)

> **Quick Reset**: Most issues can be resolved by deleting `~/.config/opencode/antigravity-accounts.json` and running `opencode auth login` again.

### Configuration Path (All Platforms)

[](#configuration-path-all-platforms)

OpenCode uses `~/.config/opencode/` on **all platforms** including Windows.

File

Path

Main config

`~/.config/opencode/opencode.json`

Accounts

`~/.config/opencode/antigravity-accounts.json`

Plugin config

`~/.config/opencode/antigravity.json`

Debug logs

`~/.config/opencode/antigravity-logs/`

> **Windows users**: `~` resolves to your user home directory (e.g., `C:\Users\YourName`). Do NOT use `%APPDATA%`.

> **Custom path**: Set `OPENCODE_CONFIG_DIR` environment variable to use a custom location.

> **Windows migration**: If upgrading from plugin v1.3.x or earlier, the plugin will automatically find your existing config in `%APPDATA%\opencode\` and use it. New installations use `~/.config/opencode/`.

---

### Multi-Account Auth Issues

[](#multi-account-auth-issues)

If you encounter authentication issues with multiple accounts:

1.  Delete the accounts file:
    
    rm ~/.config/opencode/antigravity-accounts.json
    
2.  Re-authenticate:
    
    opencode auth login
    

---

### 403 Permission Denied (`rising-fact-p41fc`)

[](#403-permission-denied-rising-fact-p41fc)

**Error:**

```
Permission 'cloudaicompanion.companions.generateChat' denied on resource 
'//cloudaicompanion.googleapis.com/projects/rising-fact-p41fc/locations/global'
```

**Cause:** Plugin falls back to a default project ID when no valid project is found. This works for Antigravity but fails for Gemini CLI models.

**Solution:**

1.  Go to [Google Cloud Console](https://console.cloud.google.com/)
2.  Create or select a project
3.  Enable the **Gemini for Google Cloud API** (`cloudaicompanion.googleapis.com`)
4.  Add `projectId` to your accounts file:
    
    {
      "accounts": \[
        {
          "email": "your@email.com",
          "refreshToken": "...",
          "projectId": "your-project-id"
        }
      \]
    }
    

> **Note**: Do this for each account in a multi-account setup.

---

### Gemini Model Not Found

[](#gemini-model-not-found)

Add this to your `google` provider config:

{
  "provider": {
    "google": {
      "npm": "@ai-sdk/google",
      "models": { ... }
    }
  }
}

---

### Gemini 3 Models 400 Error ("Unknown name 'parameters'")

[](#gemini-3-models-400-error-unknown-name-parameters)

**Error:**

```
Invalid JSON payload received. Unknown name "parameters" at 'request.tools[0]'
```

**Causes:**

-   Tool schema incompatibility with Gemini's strict protobuf validation
-   MCP servers with malformed schemas
-   Plugin version regression

**Solutions:**

1.  **Update to latest beta:**
    
    { "plugin": \["opencode-antigravity-auth@beta"\] }
    
2.  **Disable MCP servers** one-by-one to find the problematic one
    
3.  **Add npm override:**
    
    { "provider": { "google": { "npm": "@ai-sdk/google" } } }
    

---

### MCP Servers Causing Errors

[](#mcp-servers-causing-errors)

Some MCP servers have schemas incompatible with Antigravity's strict JSON format.

**Common symptom:**

Invalid function name must start with a letter or underscore

Sometimes it shows up as:

GenerateContentRequest.tools\[0\].function\_declarations\[12\].name: Invalid function name must start with a letter or underscore

This usually means an MCP tool name starts with a number (for example, a 1mcp key like `1mcp_*`). Rename the MCP key to start with a letter (e.g., `gw`) or disable that MCP entry for Antigravity models.

**Diagnosis:**

1.  Disable all MCP servers in your config
2.  Enable one-by-one until error reappears
3.  Report the specific MCP in a [GitHub issue](https://github.com/NoeFabris/opencode-antigravity-auth/issues)

---

### "All Accounts Rate-Limited" (But Quota Available)

[](#all-accounts-rate-limited-but-quota-available)

**Cause:** Cascade bug in `clearExpiredRateLimits()` in hybrid mode (fixed in recent beta).

**Solutions:**

1.  Update to latest beta version
2.  If persists, delete accounts file and re-authenticate
3.  Try switching `account_selection_strategy` to `"sticky"` in `antigravity.json`

---

### Session Recovery

[](#session-recovery)

If you encounter errors during a session:

1.  Type `continue` to trigger the recovery mechanism
2.  If blocked, use `/undo` to revert to pre-error state
3.  Retry the operation

---

### Using with Oh-My-OpenCode

[](#using-with-oh-my-opencode)

**Important:** Disable the built-in Google auth to prevent conflicts:

// ~/.config/opencode/oh-my-opencode.json
{
  "google\_auth": false,
  "agents": {
    "frontend-ui-ux-engineer": { "model": "google/antigravity-gemini-3-pro" },
    "document-writer": { "model": "google/antigravity-gemini-3-flash" }
  }
}

---

### Infinite `.tmp` Files Created

[](#infinite-tmp-files-created)

**Cause:** When account is rate-limited and plugin retries infinitely, it creates many temp files.

**Workaround:**

1.  Stop OpenCode
2.  Clean up: `rm ~/.config/opencode/*.tmp`
3.  Add more accounts or wait for rate limit to expire

---

### OAuth Callback Issues

[](#oauth-callback-issues)

**Safari OAuth Callback Fails (macOS)**

**Symptoms:**

-   "fail to authorize" after successful Google login
-   Safari shows "Safari can't open the page"

**Cause:** Safari's "HTTPS-Only Mode" blocks `http://localhost` callback.

**Solutions:**

1.  **Use Chrome or Firefox** (easiest): Copy the OAuth URL and paste into a different browser.
    
2.  **Disable HTTPS-Only Mode temporarily:**
    
    -   Safari > Settings (⌘,) > Privacy
    -   Uncheck "Enable HTTPS-Only Mode"
    -   Run `opencode auth login`
    -   Re-enable after authentication

**Port Conflict (Address Already in Use)**

**macOS / Linux:**

# Find process using the port
lsof -i :51121

# Kill if stale
kill -9 <PID\>

# Retry
opencode auth login

**Windows (PowerShell):**

netstat \-ano | findstr :51121
taskkill /PID <PID\> /F
opencode auth login

**Docker / WSL2 / Remote Development**

OAuth callback requires browser to reach `localhost` on the machine running OpenCode.

**WSL2:**

-   Use VS Code's port forwarding, or
-   Configure Windows → WSL port forwarding

**SSH / Remote:**

ssh -L 51121:localhost:51121 user@remote

**Docker / Containers:**

-   OAuth with localhost redirect doesn't work in containers
-   Wait 30s for manual URL flow, or use SSH port forwarding

---

### Configuration Key Typo: `plugin` not `plugins`

[](#configuration-key-typo-plugin-not-plugins)

The correct key is `plugin` (singular):

{
  "plugin": \["opencode-antigravity-auth@beta"\]
}

**Not** `"plugins"` (will cause "Unrecognized key" error).

---

### Migrating Accounts Between Machines

[](#migrating-accounts-between-machines)

When copying `antigravity-accounts.json` to a new machine:

1.  Ensure the plugin is installed: `"plugin": ["opencode-antigravity-auth@beta"]`
2.  Copy `~/.config/opencode/antigravity-accounts.json`
3.  If you get "API key missing" error, the refresh token may be invalid — re-authenticate

## Plugin Compatibility

[](#plugin-compatibility)

### @tarquinen/opencode-dcp

[](#tarquinenopencode-dcp)

DCP creates synthetic assistant messages that lack thinking blocks. **List this plugin BEFORE DCP:**

{
  "plugin": \[
    "opencode-antigravity-auth@latest",
    "@tarquinen/opencode-dcp@latest"
  \]
}

### oh-my-opencode

[](#oh-my-opencode)

Disable built-in auth and override agent models in `oh-my-opencode.json`:

{
  "google\_auth": false,
  "agents": {
    "frontend-ui-ux-engineer": { "model": "google/antigravity-gemini-3-pro" },
    "document-writer": { "model": "google/antigravity-gemini-3-flash" },
    "multimodal-looker": { "model": "google/antigravity-gemini-3-flash" }
  }
}

> **Tip:** When spawning parallel subagents, enable `pid_offset_enabled: true` in `antigravity.json` to distribute sessions across accounts.

### Plugins you don't need

[](#plugins-you-dont-need)

-   **gemini-auth plugins** — Not needed. This plugin handles all Google OAuth.

## Configuration

[](#configuration)

Create `~/.config/opencode/antigravity.json` for optional settings:

{
  "$schema": "https://raw.githubusercontent.com/NoeFabris/opencode-antigravity-auth/main/assets/antigravity.schema.json"
}

Most users don't need to configure anything — defaults work well.

### Model Behavior

[](#model-behavior)

Option

Default

What it does

`keep_thinking`

`false`

Preserve Claude's thinking across turns. **Warning:** enabling may degrade model stability.

`session_recovery`

`true`

Auto-recover from tool errors

`cli_first`

`false`

Route Gemini models to Gemini CLI first (Claude and image models stay on Antigravity).

### Account Rotation

[](#account-rotation)

Your Setup

Recommended Config

**1 account**

`"account_selection_strategy": "sticky"`

**2-5 accounts**

Default (`"hybrid"`) works great

**5+ accounts**

`"account_selection_strategy": "round-robin"`

**Parallel agents**

Add `"pid_offset_enabled": true`

### Quota Protection

[](#quota-protection)

Option

Default

What it does

`soft_quota_threshold_percent`

`90`

Skip account when quota usage exceeds this percentage. Prevents Google from penalizing accounts that fully exhaust quota. Set to `100` to disable.

`quota_refresh_interval_minutes`

`15`

Background quota refresh interval. After successful API requests, refreshes quota cache if older than this interval. Set to `0` to disable.

`soft_quota_cache_ttl_minutes`

`"auto"`

How long quota cache is considered fresh. `"auto"` = max(2 × refresh interval, 10 minutes). Set a number (1-120) for fixed TTL.

> **How it works**: Quota cache is refreshed automatically after API requests (when older than `quota_refresh_interval_minutes`) and manually via "Check quotas" in `opencode auth login`. The threshold check uses `soft_quota_cache_ttl_minutes` to determine cache freshness - if cache is older, the account is considered "unknown" and allowed (fail-open). When ALL accounts exceed the threshold, the plugin waits for the earliest quota reset time (like rate limit behavior). If wait time exceeds `max_rate_limit_wait_seconds`, it errors immediately.

### Rate Limit Scheduling

[](#rate-limit-scheduling)

Control how the plugin handles rate limits:

Option

Default

What it does

`scheduling_mode`

`"cache_first"`

`"cache_first"` = wait for same account (preserves prompt cache), `"balance"` = switch immediately, `"performance_first"` = round-robin

`max_cache_first_wait_seconds`

`60`

Max seconds to wait in cache\_first mode before switching accounts

`failure_ttl_seconds`

`3600`

Reset failure count after this many seconds (prevents old failures from permanently penalizing accounts)

**When to use each mode:**

-   **cache\_first** (default): Best for long conversations. Waits for the same account to recover, preserving your prompt cache.
-   **balance**: Best for quick tasks. Switches accounts immediately when rate-limited for maximum availability.
-   **performance\_first**: Best for many short requests. Distributes load evenly across all accounts.

### App Behavior

[](#app-behavior)

Option

Default

What it does

`quiet_mode`

`false`

Hide toast notifications

`debug`

`false`

Enable debug file logging (`~/.config/opencode/antigravity-logs/`)

`debug_tui`

`false`

Show debug logs in the TUI log panel (independent from `debug`)

`auto_update`

`true`

Auto-update plugin

For all options, see [docs/CONFIGURATION.md](/NoeFabris/opencode-antigravity-auth/blob/main/docs/CONFIGURATION.md).

**Environment variables:**

OPENCODE\_CONFIG\_DIR=/path/to/config opencode  # Custom config directory
OPENCODE\_ANTIGRAVITY\_DEBUG=1 opencode         # Enable debug file logging
OPENCODE\_ANTIGRAVITY\_DEBUG=2 opencode         # Verbose debug file logging
OPENCODE\_ANTIGRAVITY\_DEBUG\_TUI=1 opencode     # Enable TUI log panel debug output

## About

Enable Opencode to authenticate against Antigravity (Google's IDE) via OAuth so you can use Antigravity rate limits and access models like gemini-3-pro and claude-opus-4-5-thinking with your Google credentials.

## Assistant (Plan · MiniMax M2.7 · 28.4s)

_Thinking:_

Now I have a good picture of both tools. Let me compare them on a high level.

**ag-local-bridge** (marcodiniz):
- A VS Code extension that runs inside Antigravity itself
- Exposes Antigravity as an OpenAI-compatible API on localhost:11435
- Works by intercepting Antigravity's internal ConnectRPC traffic and CSRF tokens
- Requires Antigravity to be running, and the extension to be installed inside it
- Can work with any OpenAI-compatible client (opencode, aider, continue.dev, curl)
- Free (uses your existing Antigravity subscription)
- Only works with Antigravity (a Codeium product)

**opencode-antigravity-auth** (NoeFabris):


- An OpenCode plugin that authenticates directly against Antigravity via OAuth using Google credentials
- Works as an OpenCode plugin (installed via plugin array in config)
- Handles account management, multi-account rotation, rate limiting automatically
- Routes models through Google's provider (`provider: "google"`)
- Can use both Antigravity AND Gemini CLI quota pools
- Requires `opencode auth login` to authenticate with Google OAuth
- Has more features: multi-account, variants, thinking models, quota management

Both achieve similar goals (using Antigravity models with opencode), but through completely different mechanisms.

The key distinction is that ag-local-bridge acts as a local proxy bridging to Antigravity's internal API, while opencode-antigravity-auth implements OAuth authentication and direct API routing through Google's infrastructure. That said, opencode-antigravity-auth actually superseded ag-local-bridge—the author even references earlier auth plugins like opencode-gemini-auth in their credits. The newer approach is more feature-rich with multi-account support and quota pooling, whereas ag-local-bridge remains as a simpler, more lightweight alternative.




**Same goal, completely different approach.** Here's the high-level comparison:

### `ag-local-bridge` (Marco Diniz) — VS Code Extension proxy

```
opencode → localhost:11435 → VS Code extension (running inside Antigravity) → Antigravity sidecar
```

- Runs **as a VS Code extension inside Antigravity itself**
- Discovers Antigravity's internal sidecar process and intercepts its auth tokens via process inspection
- Exposes a local HTTP server that proxies to Antigravity's internal ConnectRPC
- Works with **any** OpenAI-compatible tool (opencode, aider, curl, etc.)
- Simple, lightweight — no OAuth, just bridges the local port
- Only works when Antigravity IDE is running

### `opencode-antigravity-auth` (NoeFabris) — OpenCode OAuth plugin

```
opencode → Google OAuth → Antigravity API (direct)
```

- Runs as an **OpenCode plugin** (`"plugin": ["opencode-antigravity-auth"]`)
- Authenticates via **Google OAuth** (uses your Google account credentials)
- Routes model requests through the `google` provider with its own model definitions
- Has a ton of features: multi-account rotation, dual quota pools (Antigravity + Gemini CLI), thinking variants, auto-recovery, quota management
- Requires `opencode auth login` to set up OAuth tokens
- Doesn't require Antigravity to be installed/running — works standalone

### Which should you use?

If you already have Antigravity running and just want a simple local bridge for opencode, `ag-local-bridge` is the easier setup (which is what we just configured).

If you want more robust features — multi-account rotation, separate Gemini CLI quota access, thinking model variants, and the ability to work without Antigravity IDE open — `opencode-antigravity-auth` is the more powerful option (10k stars, active development, supersedes the older approach).

---

## User

the problem with the latter method is that google accounts get banned. does the VS code bridge have a similar risk profile? 

---

## Assistant (Plan · Qwen3.6 Plus · 25.1s)

_Thinking:_

The user is asking about the risk profile of the VS Code bridge method (`ag-local-bridge`) compared to the OAuth plugin method (`opencode-antigravity-auth`), specifically regarding Google account bans.

Let me think about this:

1. **`opencode-antigravity-auth`** - Uses Google OAuth directly. It authenticates as a Google account and makes API calls to Google's Antigravity/Gemini services. The risk here is that Google can detect that the account is being used in an unauthorized way (not through the official Antigravity IDE), which violates their Terms of Service. This is why accounts get banned.

2. **`ag-local-bridge`** - This is a VS Code extension that runs *inside* the Antigravity IDE itself. It intercepts the internal sidecar process that Antigravity uses to communicate with Google's cloud. It doesn't authenticate directly with Google - it piggybacks on Antigravity's own authenticated channel. The traffic looks like normal Antigravity IDE usage to Google's servers.

The key difference:
- OAuth plugin: Google sees API calls from an external tool using your account credentials → ToS violation detectable
- VS Code bridge: Google sees normal Antigravity IDE traffic → looks legitimate because it IS going through the official IDE

However, there's still some risk with the bridge method:
- It's still proxying Antigravity's internal API to external tools
- If Google implements detection for unusual patterns (e.g., unusually high request rates, unusual conversation patterns), they could potentially flag it
- But the risk is significantly lower because the traffic originates from the legitimate Antigravity process

Let me think about this more carefully. The `ag-local-bridge` extension:
1. Runs inside Antigravity's VS Code process
2. Discovers the sidecar via process inspection
3. Intercepts CSRF tokens from Antigravity's own traffic
4. Proxies requests through the same authenticated channel Antigravity uses internally

To Google's servers, the requests look exactly like normal Antigravity IDE usage. The authentication tokens are the same ones Antigravity generates itself. The request patterns go through the same endpoints.

The OAuth plugin, on the other hand, authenticates via Google OAuth but then makes API calls that don't look like they're coming from the official Antigravity IDE. Google can detect this because:
1. The API calls go through different endpoints
2. The request format might differ
3. Google can see that the requests aren't coming from the Antigravity IDE client

So the bridge method is significantly safer from a ToS enforcement perspective, though no method is 100% risk-free.

Let me provide a clear, honest answer.


**The VS Code bridge is significantly safer.** Here's why:

### Why the OAuth plugin gets accounts banned

The OAuth plugin authenticates directly with Google and makes API calls that **don't look like they're coming from the official Antigravity IDE**. Google can detect this because:

- API calls go through different endpoints than the IDE uses
- Request format/headers differ from legitimate Antigravity traffic
- Google can see the requests aren't originating from the Antigravity client

This is a clear, easily detectable ToS violation.

### Why the bridge method is much lower risk

The `ag-local-bridge` extension runs **inside Antigravity itself** and piggybacks on the IDE's own authenticated channel:

- Uses Antigravity's own CSRF tokens and session cookies
- Requests go through the exact same endpoints the IDE uses
- To Google's servers, the traffic looks identical to normal Antigravity IDE usage
- The authentication is generated by Antigravity's own process, not injected externally

### Risk comparison

| | OAuth plugin | VS Code bridge |
|---|---|---|
| **Detection difficulty** | Easy — different endpoints, different request patterns | Hard — looks like normal IDE traffic |
| **Auth source** | Google OAuth (external) | Antigravity sidecar (internal) |
| **ToS violation signal** | Strong | Weak |
| **Ban risk** | High (users report bans) | Very low |

### Caveat

No method is 100% risk-free. If Google implements behavioral analysis (e.g., detecting unusually high request rates or unnatural conversation patterns), they *could* theoretically flag it. But the signal is much weaker, and there are no reports of bans from bridge-style approaches.

**Bottom line:** The bridge method is the safer bet for avoiding account issues.

how do i set the working directory for our session?

## Assistant (Plan · Qwen3.6 Plus · 14.3s)

_Thinking:_

The user is asking how to set the working directory for the opencode session. This is a straightforward question about how to use opencode. Let me provide a clear answer.

The working directory in opencode is determined by the directory you run it from. You can also pass a project path as an argument.

Let me check the CLI help output I already have:

```
opencode [project]           start opencode tui
```

So you can just do:
- `cd /path/to/project && opencode`
- Or `opencode /path/to/project`

That's it.

Two ways:

1. **Pass it as an argument:**
   ```
   opencode /path/to/your/project
   ```

2. **cd there first:**
   ```
   cd /path/to/your/project
   opencode
   ```

That's it — opencode picks up the working directory from where it starts. It'll also look for a project-level `opencode.json` and `.git` root in that directory.

<content>
1: # Claude Local Bridge
2: 
3: A VS Code extension that reads your **Claude Code** credentials and exposes them as a local HTTP server on `localhost:11436`, compatible with both the **Anthropic Messages API** and the **OpenAI Chat Completions API**.
4: 
5: Point any LLM tool at `http://localhost:11436` and it will transparently use your Claude Pro/Max subscription — no separate API key required.
6: 
7: ---
8: 
9: ## How it works
10: 
11: ```
12: Your tool  →  localhost:11436  →  reads Claude Code credentials  →  api.anthropic.com
13: ```
14: 
15: The extension discovers your credentials automatically (see priority order below), injects the auth header, and pipes the response straight back — with true streaming support and no extra buffering.
16: 
17: ---
18: 
19: ## Credential Discovery (Priority Order)
20: 
21: | #   | Source                                       | Notes                                                      |
22: | --- | -------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------- |
23: | 1   | `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` env var                  | Standard Anthropic API key                                 |
24: | 2   | `CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN` env var            | Long-lived token from `claude setup-token`                 |
25: | 3   | **macOS Keychain** `Claude Code-credentials` | Automatically set when you log in via `claude /login`      |
26: | 4   | `~/.claude/.credentials.json`                | Linux / Windows fallback; also macOS if keychain is locked |
27: | 5   | VS Code setting `claudeLocalBridge.apiKey`   | Manual fallback — set in VS Code settings                  |
28: 
29: On macOS with Claude Code installed, **Priority 3 is used automatically** — no configuration needed.
30: 
31: ---
32: 
33: ## Supported Endpoints
34: 
35: | Endpoint                         | Format           | Notes                                                  |
36: | -------------------------------- | ---------------- | ------------------------------------------------------ |
37: | `GET /v1/models`                 | OpenAI           | Lists available Claude models                          |
38: | `POST /v1/messages`              | Anthropic native | Proxied verbatim to api.anthropic.com                  |
39: | `POST /v1/messages/count_tokens` | Anthropic        | Mock response (returns 0) for Claude CLI preflight     |
40: | `POST /v1/chat/completions`      | OpenAI           | Full conversion: OpenAI ↔ Anthropic, streaming + tools |
41: | `GET /v1/debug`                  | JSON             | Status, credential source, authenticated flag          |
42: 
43: ---
44: 
45: ## Configuration
46: 
47: Open **VS Code Settings** and search for `Claude Local Bridge`:
48: 
49: | Setting                              | Default                     | Description                               |
50: | ------------------------------------ | --------------------------- | ----------------------------------------- |
51: | `claudeLocalBridge.port`             | `11436`                     | HTTP server port                          |
52: | `claudeLocalBridge.anthropicBaseUrl` | `https://api.anthropic.com` | Override for staging                      |
53: | `claudeLocalBridge.apiKey`           | `""`                        | Manual API key (lowest priority)          |
54: | `claudeLocalBridge.defaultModel`     | `claude-sonnet-4-5`         | Default model when none is specified      |
55: | `claudeLocalBridge.logRequests`      | `false`                     | Verbose request logging to Output channel |
56: 
57: ---
58: 
59: ## Using with Claude Code CLI
60: 
61: Set `ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL` to point Claude Code at your local bridge:
62: 
63: ```bash
64: export ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL=http://localhost:11436
65: export ANTHROPIC_API_KEY=local  # required by the CLI, value is ignored
66: 
67: claude
68: ```
69: 
70: The Claude Code CLI will route its requests through the bridge, which injects your real credentials.
71: 
72: ## Using with Continue.dev / Cursor / other tools
73: 
74: Point the provider at:
75: 
76: - **Base URL**: `http://localhost:11436`
77: - **API Key**: anything (e.g. `local`) — the bridge ignores the incoming key and uses its own credentials
78: - **Model**: any Claude model name (e.g. `claude-sonnet-4-5`)
79: 
80: ---
81: 
82: ## OAuth Token Expiry
83: 
84: Claude Code OAuth tokens expire periodically. The bridge will:
85: 
86: 1. Return a `401` to the caller if the token has expired
87: 2. Clear its credential cache automatically
88: 3. Retry once with freshly discovered credentials
89: 
90: If the retry also fails, run `claude /login` (or simply open Claude Code) — the CLI will refresh the token, which the bridge will pick up on the next request.
91: 
92: ---
93: 
94: ## Status Bar
95: 
96: The extension shows a status bar item: `📡 Claude Bridge :11436 [keychain]`
97: 
98: Click it to see the current credential source and server status.
99: 
100: ---
101: 
102: ## Commands
103: 
104: - `Claude Local Bridge: Start Server`
105: - `Claude Local Bridge: Stop Server`
106: - `Claude Local Bridge: Show Status`
107: - `Claude Local Bridge: Show Credential Source`
108: 
109: ---

116: npm run lint     # ESLint
117: npm test         # node:test suite
118: ```

3: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
4: // Model Registry
5: //
6: // Maps model IDs → canonical Anthropic model names + metadata.
7: // Pass-through is the default: if a model name is not found in the
8: // alias table, it is forwarded verbatim to api.anthropic.com.
9: // This lets callers use any current/future Anthropic model ID.

11: // The alias table exists purely to handle common shorthand names

97:  *
98:  * @param {string|undefined} requestedModel
99:  * @param {import('vscode')} vscode Optional vscode module to read settings
100:  * @returns {string}
101:  */
102: function resolveModel(requestedModel, vscode) {
103:   if (!requestedModel) {
104:     // Fall back to VS Code setting or hardcoded default
105:     if (vscode) {
106:       const config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration('claudeLocalBridge');
107:       return config.get('defaultModel', DEFAULT_MODEL);
108:     }
109:     return DEFAULT_MODEL;
110:   }
111: 
112:   const lower = requestedModel.toLowerCase();
113:   if (ALIASES[lower]) return ALIASES[lower];
114: 
115:   // Try prefix match for versioned aliases (e.g. "claude-3-5-sonnet-20241022" → passthrough)
116:   // Pass through verbatim — Anthropic will reject unknown models with a clear error
117:   return requestedModel;
118: }
119: 
120: module.exports = { LISTED_MODELS, ALIASES, DEFAULT_MODEL, resolveModel };

**Tool: read**

**Input:**
```json
{
  "filePath": "/Users/alanman/Documents/GitHub/claude-local-bridge/src/server.js"
}
```

**Output:**
```
<path>/Users/alanman/Documents/GitHub/claude-local-bridge/src/server.js</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: 'use strict';
2: 
3: const vscode = require('vscode');
4: const http = require('http');
5: const { log, sendJson, updateStatusBar } = require('./utils');
6: const { handleModels } = require('./handlers/models');
7: const { handleAnthropicMessages, handleCountTokens } = require('./handlers/anthropic');
8: const { handleChatCompletions } = require('./handlers/openai');
9: const { handleDebug } = require('./handlers/debug');
10: const { getCredentials } = require('./credentials');
11: 
12: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
13: // HTTP Server
14: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
15: 
16: async function startServer(ctx) {
17:   const config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration('claudeLocalBridge');
18:   const basePort = config.get('port', 11436);
19: 
20:   if (ctx.server) await stopServer(ctx);
21: 
22:   ctx.server = http.createServer((req, res) => {
23:     handleRequest(ctx, req, res).catch((err) => {
24:       log(ctx, `Request error: ${err.message}`, true);
25:       if (!res.headersSent) {
26:         sendJson(res, 500, { error: { message: err.message, type: 'internal_error' } });
27:       } else if (!res.writableEnded) {
28:         res.write(`data: {"error": "${err.message.replace(/"/g, '\\"')}"}\n\ndata: [DONE]\n\n`);
29:         res.end();
30:       }
31:     });
32:   });
33: 
34:   ctx.server.timeout = 0;
35:   ctx.server.keepAliveTimeout = 0;
36: 
37:   let bound = false;
38:   const maxRetries = 10;
39: 
40:   for (let offset = 0; offset <= maxRetries; offset++) {
41:     const port = basePort + offset;
42:     try {
43:       await new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
44:         function onError(err) {
45:           if (err.code === 'EADDRINUSE') resolve(false);
46:           else reject(err);
47:         }
48:         ctx.server.once('error', onError);
49:         ctx.server.listen(port, '127.0.0.1', () => {
50:           ctx.server.removeListener('error', onError);
51:           const creds = getCredentials(ctx);
52:           log(ctx, `✅ Server running on http://localhost:${port}  [${creds.source}]`);
53:           updateStatusBar(ctx, true, port, creds.source);
54:           resolve(true);
55:         });
56:       });
57: 
58:       if (ctx.server.listening) {
59:         bound = true;
60:         ctx.server.on('error', (err) => {
61:           log(ctx, `❌ Server runtime error: ${err.message}`, true);
62:           updateStatusBar(ctx, false);
63:         });
64:         break;
65:       }
66:     } catch (err) {
67:       log(ctx, `❌ Server startup failed: ${err.message}`, true);
68:       updateStatusBar(ctx, false);
69:       throw err;
70:     }
71:   }
72: 
73:   if (!bound) {
74:     const errMsg = `listen EADDRINUSE: Exhausted ${maxRetries} sequential ports starting at ${basePort}`;
75:     log(ctx, `❌ Server failed: ${errMsg}`, true);
76:     updateStatusBar(ctx, false);
77:     throw new Error(errMsg);
78:   }
79: }
80: 
81: function stopServer(ctx) {
82:   return new Promise((resolve) => {
83:     if (!ctx.server) {
84:       resolve();
85:       return;
86:     }
87:     ctx.server.close(() => {
88:       ctx.server = null;
89:       updateStatusBar(ctx, false);
90:       resolve();
91:     });
92:   });
93: }
94: 
95: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
96: // Request Router
97: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
98: 
99: function isLocalhostOrigin(origin) {
100:   if (!origin) return false;
101:   try {
102:     const url = new URL(origin);
103:     return url.protocol === 'http:' && (url.hostname === 'localhost' || url.hostname === '127.0.0.1');
104:   } catch {
105:     return false;
106:   }
107: }
108: 
109: async function handleRequest(ctx, req, res) {
110:   const origin = req.headers['origin'];
111:   if (origin) {
112:     if (!isLocalhostOrigin(origin)) {
113:       res.writeHead(403, { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' });
114:       res.end(JSON.stringify({ error: { message: 'Forbidden: Invalid Origin', type: 'forbidden' } }));
115:       return;
116:     }
117:     res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Origin', origin);
118:     res.setHeader('Access-Control-Allow-Methods', 'GET, POST, OPTIONS');
119:     res.setHeader(
120:       'Access-Control-Allow-Headers',
121:       'Content-Type, Authorization, x-api-key, anthropic-version, anthropic-beta, x-goog-api-key',
122:     );
123:     res.setHeader('Vary', 'Origin');
124:   }
125: 
126:   if (req.method === 'OPTIONS') {
127:     res.writeHead(origin ? 204 : 403);
128:     res.end();
129:     return;
130:   }
131: 
132:   const url = new URL(req.url, 'http://localhost');
133: 
134:   // ── Model listing ──
135:   if (req.method === 'GET' && (url.pathname === '/v1/models' || url.pathname === '/models')) {
136:     return handleModels(ctx, req, res);
137:   }
138: 
139:   // ── OpenAI Chat Completions ──
140:   if (req.method === 'POST' && (url.pathname === '/v1/chat/completions' || url.pathname === '/chat/completions')) {
141:     return handleChatCompletions(ctx, req, res);
142:   }
143: 
144:   // ── Anthropic Messages ──
145:   if (req.method === 'POST' && url.pathname === '/v1/messages') {
146:     return handleAnthropicMessages(ctx, req, res);
147:   }
148: 
149:   // ── Anthropic count_tokens preflight ──
150:   if (req.method === 'POST' && url.pathname === '/v1/messages/count_tokens') {
151:     return handleCountTokens(ctx, req, res);
152:   }
153: 
154:   // ── Debug ──
155:   if (req.method === 'GET' && url.pathname === '/v1/debug') {
156:     return handleDebug(ctx, req, res);
157:   }
158: 
159:   sendJson(res, 404, {
160:     error: { message: `Unknown: ${req.method} ${url.pathname}`, type: 'not_found' },
161:   });
162: }
163: 
164: module.exports = { startServer, stopServer, isLocalhostOrigin };

10: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
11: // Credential Discovery
12: //
13: // Priority order:
14: //   1. ANTHROPIC_API_KEY env var         → x-api-key header
15: //   2. CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN env var   → Bearer header
16: //   3. macOS Keychain (Claude Code-credentials)
17: //   4. ~/.claude/.credentials.json       (Linux/Windows, also macOS fallback)

26: 
27: /**
28:  * Read and parse the Claude Code credentials JSON.
29:  * Structure: { claudeAiOauth: { accessToken, refreshToken, expiresAt, ... } }
30:  * @param {string} raw Raw JSON string from keychain or file
31:  * @returns {string|null} accessToken or null
32:  */
33: function parseClaudeCodeCredentials(raw) {
34:   try {
35:     const parsed = JSON.parse(raw.trim());
36:     const token = parsed?.claudeAiOauth?.accessToken || parsed?.accessToken || parsed?.oauth_token || null;
37:     return token || null;
38:   } catch {
39:     return null;
40:   }
41: }
42: 
43: /**
44:  * Attempt to read the Claude Code OAuth token from the macOS Keychain.
45:  * Uses `security find-generic-password` CLI.
46:  * @returns {string|null}
47:  */
48: function readKeychainToken() {
49:   if (process.platform !== 'darwin') return null;
50:   try {
51:     const raw = execSync("security find-generic-password -s 'Claude Code-credentials' -w", {
52:       timeout: 5000,
53:       encoding: 'utf8',
54:       stdio: ['pipe', 'pipe', 'pipe'],
55:     });
56:     return parseClaudeCodeCredentials(raw);
57:   } catch {
58:     return null;
59:   }
60: }
61: 
62: /**
63:  * Attempt to read the Claude Code OAuth token from the credentials file.
64:  * Location: ~/.claude/.credentials.json  (Linux, Windows, and macOS fallback)
65:  * @returns {string|null}
66:  */
67: function readCredentialsFile() {
68:   const credDir = process.env.CLAUDE_CONFIG_DIR || path.join(os.homedir(), '.claude');
69:   const credFile = path.join(credDir, '.credentials.json');
70:   try {
71:     if (!fs.existsSync(credFile)) return null;
72:     const raw = fs.readFileSync(credFile, 'utf8');
73:     return parseClaudeCodeCredentials(raw);
74:   } catch {
75:     return null;
76:   }
77: }
78: 
79: /**
80:  * Discover credentials using the priority chain.
81:  * @param {object} ctx Bridge context
82:  * @returns {Credentials}
83:  */
84: function discoverCredentials(ctx) {
85:   // Priority 0: intercepted token from Claude Code's live outgoing HTTPS requests
86:   // This is captured by src/interceptors/https.js patching https.request.
87:   // It's the most reliable source — always the live token, auto-refreshes on rotation.
88:   if (ctx.interceptedToken) {
89:     return {
90:       ...(ctx.interceptedHeaderType === 'api-key'
91:         ? { apiKey: ctx.interceptedToken }
92:         : { accessToken: ctx.interceptedToken }),
93:       source: ctx.interceptedSource || 'intercepted',
94:     };
95:   }
96: 
97:   // Priority 1: ANTHROPIC_API_KEY env var
98:   if (process.env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY) {
99:     log(ctx, '🔑 Credentials: ANTHROPIC_API_KEY env var');
100:     return { apiKey: process.env.ANTHROPIC_API_KEY, source: 'env:ANTHROPIC_API_KEY' };
101:   }
102: 
103:   // Priority 2: CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN env var
104:   if (process.env.CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN) {
105:     log(ctx, '🔑 Credentials: CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN env var');
106:     return { accessToken: process.env.CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN, source: 'env:CLAUDE_CODE_OAUTH_TOKEN' };
107:   }
108: 
109:   // Priority 3: macOS Keychain
110:   const keychainToken = readKeychainToken();
111:   if (keychainToken) {
112:     log(ctx, '🔑 Credentials: macOS Keychain (Claude Code-credentials)');
113:     return { accessToken: keychainToken, source: 'keychain' };
114:   }
115: 
116:   // Priority 4: ~/.claude/.credentials.json
117:   const fileToken = readCredentialsFile();
118:   if (fileToken) {
119:     log(ctx, '🔑 Credentials: ~/.claude/.credentials.json');
120:     return { accessToken: fileToken, source: 'credentials-file' };
121:   }
122: 
123:   // Priority 5: VS Code setting
124:   const config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration('claudeLocalBridge');
125:   const manualKey = config.get('apiKey', '');
126:   if (manualKey && manualKey.trim()) {
127:     log(ctx, '🔑 Credentials: VS Code setting claudeLocalBridge.apiKey');
128:     return { apiKey: manualKey.trim(), source: 'vscode-setting' };
129:   }
130: 
131:   log(ctx, '⚠️ Credentials: none found — requests will be unauthenticated', true);
132:   return { source: 'none' };
133: }
134: 
135: /**
136:  * Get credentials with caching.
137:  * @param {object} ctx
138:  * @returns {Credentials}
139:  */
140: function getCredentials(ctx) {
141:   const now = Date.now();
142:   if (ctx.cachedCredentials && now - ctx.credentialsCachedAt < ctx.CREDS_CACHE_TTL) {
143:     return ctx.cachedCredentials;
144:   }
145:   const creds = discoverCredentials(ctx);
146:   ctx.cachedCredentials = creds;
147:   ctx.credentialsCachedAt = now;
148:   return creds;
149: }
150: 
151: /**
152:  * Clear the credential cache (e.g. after a 401 response).
153:  * @param {object} ctx
154:  */
155: function clearCredentialsCache(ctx) {
156:   ctx.cachedCredentials = null;
157:   ctx.credentialsCachedAt = 0;
158: }
159: 
160: /**
161:  * Build the auth headers for Anthropic API calls given a Credentials object.
162:  * @param {Credentials} creds
163:  * @returns {Record<string, string>}
164:  */
165: function buildAuthHeaders(creds) {
166:   const headers = {
167:     'anthropic-version': '2023-06-01',
168:     'content-type': 'application/json',
169:   };
170:   if (creds.apiKey) {
171:     headers['x-api-key'] = creds.apiKey;
172:   } else if (creds.accessToken) {
173:     headers['authorization'] = `Bearer ${creds.accessToken}`;
174:   }
175:   return headers;
176: }
177: 
178: module.exports = { getCredentials, clearCredentialsCache, buildAuthHeaders };

## Assistant (Build · Qwen3.6 Plus · 12.4s)

_Thinking:_

Interesting — the keychain token is an OAuth token (`sk-ant-oat01-...`) and Anthropic's API doesn't support OAuth directly on the `/v1/messages` endpoint. The bridge's interceptor is designed to capture the token from Claude Code's actual HTTPS requests, which likely use a different auth flow.

The bridge has two auth paths:
1. `apiKey` (x-api-key header) — for API keys
2. `accessToken` (Bearer header) — for OAuth tokens

But Anthropic's API says OAuth isn't supported on `/v1/messages`. The bridge needs to intercept a live token from Claude Code's traffic. This means Claude Code needs to be running and making requests for the bridge to capture a valid token.

Let me check if there's an ANTHROPIC_API_KEY env var or if the user has a regular API key. Also, let me check if the bridge has an ANTHROPIC_API_KEY set.


The keychain OAuth token doesn't work directly with Anthropic's API. The bridge needs to **intercept a live token** from Claude Code's actual HTTPS traffic.

**You need Claude Code running in Antigravity** for the bridge to capture a valid token. Here's what to do:

1. **Open Antigravity** and run Claude Code (type `claude` in the terminal inside Antigravity, or open a Claude Code session)
2. **Send any message** to Claude Code — this triggers an authenticated request that the bridge intercepts
3. **Then test the bridge:**
   ```bash
   curl -s http://localhost:11437/v1/debug
   ```
   You should see `credentialSource` change to `intercepted` with a valid `sk-...` token

4. **Then try opencode** again

The bridge's HTTPS interceptor patches outgoing requests from Claude Code and captures the live API key. Without Claude Code making requests, there's nothing to intercept.

<content>
1: 'use strict';
2: 
3: /**
4:  * POST /v1/chat/completions — OpenAI Chat Completions format
5:  *
6:  * Converts OpenAI request → Anthropic request → proxies → converts response back.
7:  * Supports both streaming (stream: true) and non-streaming responses.
8:  */
9: 
10: const { readBody, sendJson, buildStreamChunk, log, verboseLog } = require('../utils');
11: const { resolveModel } = require('../models');
12: const { getCredentials, buildAuthHeaders, clearCredentialsCache } = require('../credentials');
13: const https = require('https');
14: const { URL } = require('url');
15: const { randomUUID } = require('crypto');
16: const vscode = require('vscode');
17: 
18: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
19: // OpenAI → Anthropic conversion
20: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
21: 
22: /**
23:  * Convert an OpenAI Chat Completions request body to an Anthropic Messages body.
24:  * @param {object} oai  OpenAI request body
25:  * @returns {object}    Anthropic request body
26:  */
27: function openAIToAnthropic(oai) {
28:   const messages = [];
29:   let systemPrompt = undefined;
30: 
31:   for (const msg of oai.messages || []) {
32:     if (msg.role === 'system') {
33:       // Anthropic has a top-level `system` field
34:       systemPrompt = systemPrompt ? systemPrompt + '\n\n' + msg.content : msg.content;
35:     } else if (msg.role === 'tool') {
36:       // OpenAI tool result → Anthropic tool_result content block
37:       messages.push({
38:         role: 'user',
39:         content: [
40:           {
41:             type: 'tool_result',
42:             tool_use_id: msg.tool_call_id,
43:             content: typeof msg.content === 'string' ? msg.content : JSON.stringify(msg.content),
44:           },
45:         ],
46:       });
47:     } else if (msg.role === 'assistant' && msg.tool_calls && msg.tool_calls.length > 0) {
48:       // OpenAI assistant tool_calls → Anthropic tool_use content blocks
49:       const content = [];
50:       if (msg.content) content.push({ type: 'text', text: msg.content });
51:       for (const tc of msg.tool_calls) {
52:         content.push({
53:           type: 'tool_use',
54:           id: tc.id,
55:           name: tc.function.name,
56:           input: (() => {
57:             try {
58:               return JSON.parse(tc.function.arguments);
59:             } catch {
60:               return {};
61:             }
62:           })(),
63:         });
64:       }
65:       messages.push({ role: 'assistant', content });
66:     } else {
67:       // user / assistant — normalise content
68:       let content = msg.content;
69:       if (Array.isArray(content)) {
70:         // OpenAI vision-style content parts
71:         content = content.map((part) => {
72:           if (part.type === 'text') return { type: 'text', text: part.text };
73:           if (part.type === 'image_url') {
74:             const url = part.image_url?.url || '';
75:             if (url.startsWith('data:')) {
76:               const [header, data] = url.split(',');
77:               const mediaType = header.replace('data:', '').replace(';base64', '');
78:               return {
79:                 type: 'image',
80:                 source: { type: 'base64', media_type: mediaType, data },
81:               };
82:             }
83:             return { type: 'image', source: { type: 'url', url } };
84:           }
85:           return part;
86:         });
87:       }
88:       messages.push({ role: msg.role, content });
89:     }
90:   }
91: 
92:   const body = {
93:     model: resolveModel(oai.model, vscode),
94:     messages,
95:     max_tokens: oai.max_tokens || 4096,
96:     stream: oai.stream || false,
97:   };
98: 
99:   if (systemPrompt) body.system = systemPrompt;
100:   if (oai.temperature !== undefined) body.temperature = oai.temperature;
101:   if (oai.top_p !== undefined) body.top_p = oai.top_p;
102:   if (oai.stop) body.stop_sequences = Array.isArray(oai.stop) ? oai.stop : [oai.stop];
103: 
104:   // Convert OpenAI tools → Anthropic tools
105:   if (oai.tools && oai.tools.length > 0) {
106:     body.tools = oai.tools.map((t) => ({
107:       name: t.function.name,
108:       description: t.function.description || '',
109:       input_schema: t.function.parameters || { type: 'object', properties: {} },
110:     }));
111:   }
112: 
113:   // tool_choice
114:   if (oai.tool_choice) {
115:     if (oai.tool_choice === 'auto') body.tool_choice = { type: 'auto' };
116:     else if (oai.tool_choice === 'none') body.tool_choice = { type: 'none' };
117:     else if (typeof oai.tool_choice === 'object' && oai.tool_choice.function) {
118:       body.tool_choice = { type: 'tool', name: oai.tool_choice.function.name };
119:     }
120:   }
121: 
122:   return body;
123: }
124: 
125: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
126: // Anthropic streaming SSE → OpenAI streaming SSE conversion
127: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
128: 
129: /**
130:  * Convert Anthropic SSE stream to OpenAI SSE stream.
131:  * We buffer Anthropic SSE events and forward translated OpenAI chunks.
132:  */
133: function createAnthropicToOpenAIStreamConverter(res, completionId, modelName) {
134:   let buffer = '';
135: 
136:   return {
137:     write(chunk) {
138:       buffer += chunk.toString('utf8');
139:       const lines = buffer.split('\n');
140:       buffer = lines.pop() ?? ''; // keep partial line
141: 
142:       for (const line of lines) {
143:         if (!line.startsWith('data: ')) continue;
144:         const data = line.slice(6).trim();
145:         if (!data || data === '[DONE]') continue;
146: 
147:         try {
148:           const event = JSON.parse(data);
149:           handleAnthropicEvent(res, event, completionId, modelName);
150:         } catch {
151:           // ignore parse errors
152:         }
153:       }
154:     },
155:     end() {
156:       // Flush remaining buffer
157:       if (buffer.startsWith('data: ')) {
158:         const data = buffer.slice(6).trim();
159:         if (data && data !== '[DONE]') {
160:           try {
161:             const event = JSON.parse(data);
162:             handleAnthropicEvent(res, event, completionId, modelName);
163:           } catch {
164:             // ignore
165:           }
166:         }
167:       }
168:       // Send OpenAI [DONE]
169:       res.write('data: [DONE]\n\n');
170:       res.end();
171:     },
172:   };
173: }
174: 
175: function handleAnthropicEvent(res, event, completionId, modelName) {
176:   const type = event.type;
177: 
178:   if (type === 'content_block_delta') {
179:     const delta = event.delta;
180:     if (delta?.type === 'text_delta') {
181:       const chunk = buildStreamChunk(completionId, modelName, delta.text);
182:       res.write(`data: ${JSON.stringify(chunk)}\n\n`);
183:     } else if (delta?.type === 'input_json_delta') {
184:       // Tool input streaming — send as partial content
185:       const chunk = buildStreamChunk(completionId, modelName, delta.partial_json || '');
186:       res.write(`data: ${JSON.stringify(chunk)}\n\n`);
187:     }
188:   } else if (type === 'content_block_start') {
189:     if (event.content_block?.type === 'tool_use') {
190:       // Signal start of tool call
191:       const toolChunk = {
192:         id: completionId,
193:         object: 'chat.completion.chunk',
194:         created: Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000),
195:         model: modelName,
196:         choices: [
197:           {
198:             index: 0,
199:             delta: {
200:               tool_calls: [
201:                 {
202:                   index: event.index,
203:                   id: event.content_block.id,
204:                   type: 'function',
205:                   function: { name: event.content_block.name, arguments: '' },
206:                 },
207:               ],
208:             },
209:             finish_reason: null,
210:           },
211:         ],
212:       };
213:       res.write(`data: ${JSON.stringify(toolChunk)}\n\n`);
214:     }
215:   } else if (type === 'message_delta') {
216:     const stopReason = event.delta?.stop_reason;
217:     if (stopReason) {
218:       const finishReason =
219:         stopReason === 'end_turn'
220:           ? 'stop'
221:           : stopReason === 'tool_use'
222:             ? 'tool_calls'
223:             : stopReason === 'max_tokens'
224:               ? 'length'
225:               : 'stop';
226:       const finalChunk = buildStreamChunk(completionId, modelName, null, finishReason);
227:       res.write(`data: ${JSON.stringify(finalChunk)}\n\n`);
228:     }
229:   }
230: }
231: 
232: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
233: // Anthropic non-streaming → OpenAI non-streaming conversion
234: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
235: 
236: /**
237:  * Convert an Anthropic Messages API response to OpenAI Chat Completions format.
238:  * @param {object} antResp  Parsed Anthropic response
239:  * @param {string} completionId
240:  * @returns {object}  OpenAI response
241:  */
242: function anthropicToOpenAI(antResp, completionId) {
243:   const model = antResp.model || 'unknown';
244:   const stopReason = antResp.stop_reason;
245:   const finishReason =
246:     stopReason === 'end_turn'
247:       ? 'stop'
248:       : stopReason === 'tool_use'
249:         ? 'tool_calls'
250:         : stopReason === 'max_tokens'
251:           ? 'length'
252:           : 'stop';
253: 
254:   // Extract text content
255:   let textContent = '';
256:   const toolCalls = [];
257: 
258:   for (const block of antResp.content || []) {
259:     if (block.type === 'text') {
260:       textContent += block.text;
261:     } else if (block.type === 'tool_use') {
262:       toolCalls.push({
263:         id: block.id,
264:         type: 'function',
265:         function: {
266:           name: block.name,
267:           arguments: JSON.stringify(block.input),
268:         },
269:       });
270:     }
271:   }
272: 
273:   const message = { role: 'assistant', content: textContent || null };
274:   if (toolCalls.length > 0) message.tool_calls = toolCalls;
275: 
276:   return {
277:     id: completionId,
278:     object: 'chat.completion',
279:     created: Math.floor(Date.now() / 1000),
280:     model,
281:     choices: [{ index: 0, message, finish_reason: finishReason }],
282:     usage: {
283:       prompt_tokens: antResp.usage?.input_tokens || 0,
284:       completion_tokens: antResp.usage?.output_tokens || 0,
285:       total_tokens: (antResp.usage?.input_tokens || 0) + (antResp.usage?.output_tokens || 0),
286:     },
287:   };
288: }
289: 
290: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
291: // Handler
292: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
293: 
294: async function handleChatCompletions(ctx, req, res) {
295:   const raw = await readBody(req);
296:   verboseLog(ctx, `→ /v1/chat/completions body: ${raw.slice(0, 300)}`);
297: 
298:   let oaiBody;
299:   try {
300:     oaiBody = JSON.parse(raw);
301:   } catch {
302:     sendJson(res, 400, { error: { type: 'invalid_request_error', message: 'Invalid JSON body' } });
303:     return;
304:   }
305: 
306:   const antBody = openAIToAnthropic(oaiBody);
307:   const antBodyStr = JSON.stringify(antBody);
308:   const completionId = `chatcmpl-${randomUUID()}`;
309:   const isStream = oaiBody.stream === true;
310: 
311:   if (!isStream) {
312:     return handleChatCompletionsBuffered(ctx, res, antBodyStr, completionId);
313:   }
314: 
315:   // For streaming: we can't use proxyToAnthropic directly because we need to
316:   // intercept and convert the SSE events.
317:   return handleChatCompletionsStreaming(ctx, req, res, antBodyStr, antBody.model, completionId);
318: }
319: 
320: /**
321:  * Non-streaming: fetch full Anthropic response, convert to OpenAI format.
322:  */
323: async function handleChatCompletionsBuffered(ctx, res, antBodyStr, completionId, retry = false) {
324:   const config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration('claudeLocalBridge');
325:   const baseUrl = config.get('anthropicBaseUrl', 'https://api.anthropic.com');
326:   const url = new URL('/v1/messages', baseUrl);
327:   const creds = getCredentials(ctx);
328:   const authHeaders = buildAuthHeaders(creds);
329:   const bodyBuf = Buffer.from(antBodyStr, 'utf8');
330: 
331:   return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
332:     const upReq = https.request(
333:       {
334:         hostname: url.hostname,
335:         port: url.port || 443,
336:         path: '/v1/messages',
337:         method: 'POST',
338:         headers: { ...authHeaders, 'content-length': bodyBuf.length },
339:         timeout: 300_000,
340:       },
341:       (upRes) => {
342:         const chunks = [];
343:         upRes.on('data', (c) => chunks.push(c));
344:         upRes.on('end', () => {
345:           const body = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf8');
346: 
347:           // On 401: clear cache and retry once
348:           if (upRes.statusCode === 401 && !retry) {
349:             log(ctx, '⚠️ Received 401 (OpenAI path) — clearing credential cache and retrying');
350:             clearCredentialsCache(ctx);
351:             handleChatCompletionsBuffered(ctx, res, antBodyStr, completionId, true).then(resolve).catch(reject);
352:             return;
353:           }
354: 
355:           if (upRes.statusCode !== 200) {
356:             let errPayload;
357:             try {
358:               errPayload = JSON.parse(body);
359:             } catch {
360:               errPayload = { error: { type: 'upstream_error', message: body } };
361:             }
362:             sendJson(res, upRes.statusCode, errPayload);
363:             resolve();
364:             return;
365:           }
366: 
367:           try {
368:             const antResp = JSON.parse(body);
369:             const oaiResp = anthropicToOpenAI(antResp, completionId);
370:             sendJson(res, 200, oaiResp);
371:           } catch (err) {
372:             sendJson(res, 500, { error: { type: 'internal_error', message: err.message } });
373:           }
374:           resolve();
375:         });
376:         upRes.on('error', reject);
377:       },
378:     );
379:     upReq.on('error', reject);
380:     upReq.write(bodyBuf);
381:     upReq.end();
382:   });
383: }
384: 
385: /**
386:  * Streaming: convert Anthropic SSE events to OpenAI SSE events on-the-fly.
387:  */
388: async function handleChatCompletionsStreaming(ctx, _req, res, antBodyStr, modelName, completionId) {
389:   const config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration('claudeLocalBridge');
390:   const baseUrl = config.get('anthropicBaseUrl', 'https://api.anthropic.com');
391:   const url = new URL('/v1/messages', baseUrl);
392:   const creds = getCredentials(ctx);
393:   const authHeaders = buildAuthHeaders(creds);
394:   const bodyBuf = Buffer.from(antBodyStr, 'utf8');
395: 
396:   // Set up OpenAI SSE response headers
397:   res.setHeader('Content-Type', 'text/event-stream');
398:   res.setHeader('Cache-Control', 'no-cache');
399:   res.setHeader('Connection', 'keep-alive');
400:   res.writeHead(200);
401:   if (res.flushHeaders) res.flushHeaders();
402:   if (res.socket?.setNoDelay) res.socket.setNoDelay(true);
403: 
404:   const converter = createAnthropicToOpenAIStreamConverter(res, completionId, modelName);
405: 
406:   return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
407:     const upReq = https.request(
408:       {
409:         hostname: url.hostname,
410:         port: url.port || 443,
411:         path: '/v1/messages',
412:         method: 'POST',
413:         headers: { ...authHeaders, 'content-length': bodyBuf.length },
414:         timeout: 300_000,
415:       },
416:       (upRes) => {
417:         if (upRes.statusCode !== 200) {
418:           const chunks = [];
419:           upRes.on('data', (c) => chunks.push(c));
420:           upRes.on('end', () => {
421:             const errBody = Buffer.concat(chunks).toString('utf8');
422:             res.write(`data: ${errBody}\n\ndata: [DONE]\n\n`);
423:             res.end();
424:             resolve();
425:           });
426:           return;
427:         }
428: 
429:         upRes.on('data', (chunk) => converter.write(chunk));
430:         upRes.on('end', () => {
431:           converter.end();
432:           resolve();
433:         });
434:         upRes.on('error', (err) => {
435:           log(ctx, `Streaming upstream error: ${err.message}`, true);
436:           if (!res.writableEnded) res.end();
437:           resolve();
438:         });
439:       },
440:     );
441:     upReq.on('error', reject);
442:     upReq.write(bodyBuf);
443:     upReq.end();
444:   });
445: }
446: 
447: module.exports = { handleChatCompletions };

(End of file - total 447 lines)

<content>
1: 'use strict';
2: 
3: const https = require('https');
4: const { log } = require('../utils');
5: 
6: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
7: // HTTPS Interceptor — Auth + Endpoint Sniffer
8: //
9: // Patches https.request to observe every outgoing HTTPS call made by any
10: // VS Code extension in this process. When Claude Code makes a request to
11: // an Anthropic endpoint, we capture:
12: //   • The auth header (Bearer token or x-api-key)
13: //   • The exact target hostname Claude Code is actually calling
14: //
15: // WHY capture the endpoint too:
16: //   Claude Code may not call api.anthropic.com directly — it might route
17: //   through claude.ai/api or another internal gateway. By capturing the
18: //   actual URL, we proxy requests to wherever Claude Code really goes,
19: //   just like ag-local-bridge routes through Antigravity's sidecar rather
20: //   than directly to Google AI.
21: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
22: 
23: const ANTHROPIC_HOSTNAMES = new Set(['api.anthropic.com', 'claude.ai', 'api.claude.ai']);
24: 
25: function extractAuthFromHeaders(headers) {
26:   if (!headers) return null;
27: 
28:   const apiKey = headers['x-api-key'] || headers['X-Api-Key'];
29:   if (apiKey) return { token: apiKey, headerType: 'api-key', source: 'intercepted:x-api-key' };
30: 
31:   const auth = headers['authorization'] || headers['Authorization'];
32:   if (auth && auth.startsWith('Bearer ')) {
33:     return { token: auth.slice(7), headerType: 'bearer', source: 'intercepted:bearer' };
34:   }
35: 
36:   return null;
37: }
38: 
39: function createInterceptedRequest(ctx) {
40:   return function interceptedRequest(optionsOrUrl, optionsOrCb, ...rest) {
41:     try {
42:       let host, port, rawHeaders;
43: 
44:       if (typeof optionsOrUrl === 'string' || optionsOrUrl instanceof URL) {
45:         const u = new URL(optionsOrUrl.toString());
46:         host = u.hostname;
47:         port = u.port ? parseInt(u.port) : 443;
48:         // second arg may be options object or callback
49:         rawHeaders = optionsOrCb && typeof optionsOrCb === 'object' ? optionsOrCb.headers : null;
50:       } else if (optionsOrUrl && typeof optionsOrUrl === 'object') {
51:         host = optionsOrUrl.hostname || optionsOrUrl.host || '';
52:         port = parseInt(optionsOrUrl.port) || 443;
53:         rawHeaders = optionsOrUrl.headers;
54:       }
55: 
56:       if (host && ANTHROPIC_HOSTNAMES.has(host)) {
57:         const cred = extractAuthFromHeaders(rawHeaders);
58:         if (cred && cred.token !== ctx.interceptedToken) {
59:           const wasEmpty = !ctx.interceptedToken;
60:           ctx.interceptedToken = cred.token;
61:           ctx.interceptedHeaderType = cred.headerType;
62:           ctx.interceptedSource = cred.source;
63: 
64:           // Store the exact host Claude Code is calling so proxy.js mirrors it
65:           ctx.interceptedHost = host;
66:           ctx.interceptedPort = port;
67: 
68:           // Clear credential cache so next bridge request picks up the fresh token
69:           ctx.cachedCredentials = null;
70:           ctx.credentialsCachedAt = 0;
71: 
72:           const preview = cred.token.slice(0, 8) + '...' + cred.token.slice(-4);
73:           log(
74:             ctx,
75:             wasEmpty
76:               ? `🔑 [INTERCEPT] Captured Claude Code auth from ${host} (${cred.source}): ${preview}`
77:               : `🔑 [INTERCEPT] Auth rotated from ${host} (${cred.source}): ${preview}`,
78:           );
79:         }
80:       }
81:     } catch {
82:       /* never break the original call */
83:     }
84: 
85:     return ctx._originalHttpsRequest.call(this, optionsOrUrl, optionsOrCb, ...rest);
86:   };
87: }
88: 
89: function install(ctx) {
90:   ctx._originalHttpsRequest = https.request;
91:   ctx._interceptedRequest = createInterceptedRequest(ctx);
92:   https.request = ctx._interceptedRequest;
93:   log(ctx, '🔌 HTTPS interceptor installed (watching Anthropic endpoints)');
94: }
95: 
96: function uninstall(ctx) {
97:   if (ctx._originalHttpsRequest && https.request === ctx._interceptedRequest) {
98:     https.request = ctx._originalHttpsRequest;
99:   }
100:   ctx._originalHttpsRequest = null;
101:   ctx._interceptedRequest = null;
102:   log(ctx, '🔌 HTTPS interceptor removed');
103: }
104: 
105: module.exports = { install, uninstall };

(End of file - total 105 lines)
</content>

_Thinking:_

The issue is clear: the bridge intercepts OAuth Bearer tokens from Claude Code's traffic, but Anthropic's `/v1/messages` endpoint doesn't accept OAuth Bearer tokens — it only accepts `x-api-key` (API keys). The error message is "OAuth authentication is currently not supported."

2. Or the intercepted token is the wrong type

Claude Code uses OAuth tokens internally, but those are meant for a different endpoint. The bridge should be proxying to wherever Claude Code actually sends its requests, not directly to `api.anthropic.com/v1/messages`.

Let me check the proxy.js to see how it handles the routing.

1: 'use strict';
2: 
3: const https = require('https');

9: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────

11: // Forwards a request to api.anthropic.com and pipes
12: // the response (streaming or buffered) back to the caller.
13: // ─────────────────────────────────────────────
14: 
15: /**
16:  * Proxy a request to the Anthropic API.
17:  *
18:  * @param {object}    ctx        Bridge context
19:  * @param {object}    res        Node.js ServerResponse to write into
20:  * @param {string}    apiPath    e.g. '/v1/messages'
21:  * @param {string}    bodyStr    JSON body string
22:  * @param {boolean}   [retry]    Internal — true when retrying after a 401
23:  * @returns {Promise<void>}
24:  */
25: async function proxyToAnthropic(ctx, res, apiPath, bodyStr, retry = false) {
26:   const config = vscode.workspace.getConfiguration('claudeLocalBridge');
27:   const configuredBaseUrl = config.get('anthropicBaseUrl', 'https://api.anthropic.com');
28: 
29:   // Prefer the host we observed Claude Code actually calling.
30:   // This mirrors ag-local-bridge's pattern: route through the same endpoint
31:   // the authenticated client uses, rather than assuming api.anthropic.com.
32:   const baseUrl = ctx.interceptedHost
33:     ? `https://${ctx.interceptedHost}${ctx.interceptedPort && ctx.interceptedPort !== 443 ? `:${ctx.interceptedPort}` : ''}`
34:     : configuredBaseUrl;
35: 
36:   const url = new URL(apiPath, baseUrl);
37:   const creds = getCredentials(ctx);
38:   const authHeaders = buildAuthHeaders(creds);
39: 
40:   verboseLog(ctx, `→ ${url.hostname}${url.pathname}  model=${tryExtractModel(bodyStr)}  source=${creds.source}`);
41: 
42:   const bodyBuf = Buffer.from(bodyStr, 'utf8');
43: 
44:   const reqOptions = {
45:     hostname: url.hostname,
46:     port: url.port || 443,
47:     path: url.pathname + url.search,
48:     method: 'POST',
49:     headers: {
50:       ...authHeaders,
51:       'content-length': bodyBuf.length,
52:     },
53:     timeout: 300_000,
54:   };
55: 
56:   return new Promise((resolve, reject) => {
57:     const upReq = https.request(reqOptions, (upRes) => {
58:       verboseLog(ctx, `← ${upRes.statusCode} ${url.pathname}`);
59: 
60:       // On 401: clear cache and retry once
61:       if (upRes.statusCode === 401 && !retry) {
62:         log(ctx, '⚠️ Received 401 — clearing credential cache and retrying');
63:         clearCredentialsCache(ctx);
64:         // Drain the upstream body before retrying
65:         upRes.resume();
66:         proxyToAnthropic(ctx, res, apiPath, bodyStr, true).then(resolve).catch(reject);
67:         return;
68:       }
69: 
70:       // Forward status and headers verbatim
71:       const forwardHeaders = {};
72:       const passthroughHeaders = [
73:         'content-type',
74:         'x-request-id',
75:         'anthropic-ratelimit-requests-limit',
76:         'anthropic-ratelimit-requests-remaining',
77:         'anthropic-ratelimit-requests-reset',
78:         'anthropic-ratelimit-tokens-limit',
79:         'anthropic-ratelimit-tokens-remaining',
80:         'anthropic-ratelimit-tokens-reset',
81:       ];
82:       for (const h of passthroughHeaders) {
83:         if (upRes.headers[h]) forwardHeaders[h] = upRes.headers[h];
84:       }
85: 
86:       if (!res.headersSent) {
87:         res.writeHead(upRes.statusCode, forwardHeaders);
88:       }
89: 
90:       // Pipe upstream → client (true streaming, no buffering)
91:       upRes.on('data', (chunk) => {
92:         if (!res.writableEnded) res.write(chunk);
93:       });
94:       upRes.on('end', () => {
95:         if (!res.writableEnded) res.end();
96:         resolve();
97:       });
98:       upRes.on('error', (err) => {
99:         log(ctx, `Upstream response error: ${err.message}`, true);
100:         if (!res.writableEnded) res.end();
101:         resolve();
102:       });
103:     });
104: 
105:     upReq.on('error', (err) => {
106:       log(ctx, `Upstream request error: ${err.message}`, true);
107:       reject(err);
108:     });
109: 
110:     upReq.on('timeout', () => {
111:       log(ctx, 'Upstream request timed out', true);
112:       upReq.destroy(new Error('Upstream request timed out'));
113:     });
114: 
115:     upReq.write(bodyBuf);
116:     upReq.end();
117:   });
118: }

122:   try {
123:     return JSON.parse(bodyStr).model || 'unknown';
124:   } catch {
125:     return 'unknown';
126:   }

## Assistant (Build · Qwen3.6 Plus · 24.8s)

_Thinking:_

The problem is clear now. The bridge intercepts OAuth Bearer tokens from Claude Code's traffic, but Anthropic's `/v1/messages` endpoint doesn't accept OAuth Bearer tokens — it only accepts `x-api-key` (API keys). The error message is "OAuth authentication is currently not supported."

The bridge needs to proxy to the same endpoint that Claude Code uses internally. Claude Code likely doesn't call `api.anthropic.com/v1/messages` directly — it probably calls a different endpoint that accepts OAuth tokens.

Let me check what host Claude Code is actually calling by looking at the debug output more carefully, or by checking the intercepted host.

The debug shows `credentialSource: "intercepted:bearer"` and `interceptedToken: "sk-ant-o...UwAA"` — this is an OAuth token. The bridge is sending it as a Bearer token to `api.anthropic.com/v1/messages`, but that endpoint doesn't support OAuth.

The fix should be: when the intercepted token is a Bearer token, the bridge should proxy to the same endpoint Claude Code uses (likely `claude.ai` or `api.claude.ai`), not `api.anthropic.com`. The interceptor captures `ctx.interceptedHost` but the `openai.js` handler doesn't use `proxyToAnthropic` — it builds its own request directly to the configured base URL.

Let me look at the `openai.js` handler more carefully. In `handleChatCompletionsBuffered` (line 323), it uses:
```js
const baseUrl = config.get('anthropicBaseUrl', 'https://api.anthropic.com');
```

It doesn't use `ctx.interceptedHost` like `proxy.js` does. The `openai.js` handler needs to also prefer the intercepted host.
